It processes a shared bead queue in deterministic order, dispatching work to any headless CLI (Claude Code, OpenCode, Codex, Aider) and handling every outcome through an explicit, predefined path.\n8\t\n9\t---\n10\t\n11\t## 🧠 Core Principle\n12\t\n13\tNEEDLE is a **state machine**, not a script. Every bead transitions through a finite set of states, and every transition has a defined handler. There are no implicit fallbacks, no swallowed errors, no undefined paths.\n14\t\n15\t```\n16\tIf an outcome can happen, it has a handler.\n17\tIf it doesn't have a handler, it cannot happen.\n18\t```\n19\t\n20\t---\n21\t\n22\t## 🔄 The NEEDLE Algorithm\n23\t\n24\tA single worker executes this loop indefinitely:\n25\t\n26\t```\n27\t┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n28\t│                                                     │\n29\t│   ┌───────────┐                                     │\n30\t│   │  🔍 SELECT │◄────────────────────────────────┐  │\n31\t│   └─────┬─────┘                                  │  │\n32\t│         │                                        │  │\n33\t│         ▼                                        │  │\n34\t│   ┌───────────┐   race lost    ┌──────────┐     │  │\n35\t│   │  🔒 CLAIM  │──────────────►│ 🔁 RETRY  │─────┘  │\n36\t│   └─────┬─────┘               └──────────┘        │\n37\t│         │ claimed                                   │\n38\t│         ▼                                           │\n39\t│   ┌───────────┐                                     │\n40\t│   │ 📋 BUILD   │                                     │\n41\t│   └─────┬─────┘                                     │\n42\t│         │                                           │\n43\t│         ▼                                           │\n44\t│   ┌───────────┐                                     │\n45\t│   │ 🚀 DISPATCH│                                     │\n46\t│   └─────┬─────┘                                     │\n47\t│         │                                           │\n48\t│         ▼                                           │\n49\t│   ┌───────────┐                                     │\n50\t│   │ ⏳ EXECUTE │                                     │\n51\t│   └─────┬─────┘                                     │\n52\t│         │                                           │\n53\t│         ▼                                           │\n54\t│   ┌───────────┐                                     │\n55\t│   │ 📊 OUTCOME │                                     │\n56\t│   └─────┬─────┘                                     │\n57\t│         │                                           │\n58\t│         ├── ✅ success ──► close bead ──────────────┘\n59\t│         ├── ❌ failure ──► log + release ────────────┘\n60\t│         ├── ⏰ timeout ──► release + defer ──────────┘\n61\t│         └── 💀 crash ────► release + alert ──────────┘\n62\t│                                                     │\n63\t└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n64\t```\n65\t\n66\t---\n67\t\n68\t## 📐 Algorithm Steps\n69\t\n70\t### 🔍 Step 1: Select\n71\t\n72\tQuery the bead queue for the next claimable bead in **deterministic priority order**. Selection is not random — given the same queue state, every worker computes the same ordering. Ties are broken by creation time (oldest first).\n73\t\n74\t### 🔒 Step 2: Claim\n75\t\n76\tAttempt an **atomic claim** via `br update --claim`. SQLite transaction isolation guarantees exactly one worker succeeds. If the claim fails (race lost), return to Step 1 with the losing candidate excluded.\n77\t\n78\t### 📋 Step 3: Build\n79\t\n80\tConstruct the prompt from the bead's context: title, body, workspace path, relevant files, and any dependency context. The prompt is a deterministic function of the bead state — same bead, same prompt.\n81\t\n82\t### 🚀 Step 4: Dispatch\n83\t\n84\tLoad the agent adapter configuration (YAML), render the invoke template with the built prompt, and execute via `bash -c`. The agent runs headless — it receives a prompt, does work, and exits.\n85\t\n86\t### ⏳ Step 5: Execute\n87\t\n88\tThe agent runs. NEEDLE waits. The only inputs are the exit code and stdout/stderr. There is no interactive communication during execution.\n89\t\n90\t### 📊 Step 6: Outcome\n91\t\n92\tEvaluate the result and follow the **explicit path** for the observed outcome:\n93\t\n94\t| Outcome | Exit Code | Handler |\n95\t|---------|-----------|---------|\n96\t| ✅ **Success** | `0` | Validate output → close bead → log effort → **loop** |\n97\t| ❌ **Failure** | `1` | Log failure reason → release bead → increment retry count → **loop** |\n98\t| ⏰ **Timeout** | `124` | Release bead → mark deferred → **loop** |\n99\t| 💀 **Crash** | `>128` | Release bead → create alert bead → **loop** |\n100\t| 🏁 **Race Lost** | `4` | (Handled at Step 2) → exclude candidate → **retry select** |\n101\t| 🫙 **Queue Empty** | — | Enter strand escalation → **explore / mend / knot** |\n102\t\n103\tEvery row is implemented. There are no unhandled cases.\n104\t\n105\t---\n106\t\n107\t## 🧶 Strand Escalation\n108\t\n109\tWhen the primary workspace has no claimable beads, NEEDLE follows a **strand sequence** to find or create work. Each strand is evaluated in order — the first strand that yields a bead wins.\n110\t\n111\t| # | Strand | Agent? | Purpose |\n112\t|---|--------|--------|---------|\n113\t| 1 | 🪡 **Pluck** | Yes | Process beads from the assigned workspace |\n114\t| 2 | 🔭 **Explore** | No | Search other workspaces for claimable beads |\n115\t| 3 | 🔧 **Mend** | No | Cleanup: orphaned claims, stale locks, health checks |\n116\t| 4 | 🕸️ **Weave** | Yes | Create beads from documentation gaps *(opt-in)* |\n117\t| 5 | 🪢 **Unravel** | Yes | Propose alternatives for HUMAN-blocked beads *(opt-in)* |\n118\t| 6 | 💓 **Pulse** | Yes | Codebase health scans, auto-generate beads *(opt-in)* |\n119\t| 7 | 🪢 **Knot** | No | All strands exhausted — alert human, wait |\n120\t\n121\t---\n122\t\n123\t## ⚡ Parallel Workers\n124\t\n125\tMultiple NEEDLE workers run independently with **no central orchestrator**. Coordination happens through the shared bead queue:\n126\t\n127\t- **Atomicity** — `br update --claim` uses SQLite transactions; exactly one worker wins each claim\n128\t- **Determinism** — all workers compute the same priority order; races are resolved by the database, not by timing\n129\t- **Independence** — each worker is a self-contained loop in its own tmux session\n130\t- **Naming** — workers use NATO alphabet identifiers: `alpha`, `bravo`, `charlie`, ...\n131\t\n132\t```\n133\t  needle-claude-sonnet-alpha ──┐\n134\t  needle-claude-sonnet-bravo ──┤\n135\t  needle-codex-gpt4-charlie ───┼──► Shared .beads/ (SQLite + JSONL)\n136\t  needle-opencode-qwen-delta ──┤\n137\t  needle-aider-sonnet-echo ────┘\n138\t```\n139\t\n140\t---\n141\t\n142\t## 🏗️ Supported Agents\n143\t\n144\tNEEDLE is agent-agnostic. Any CLI that accepts a prompt and exits works.\n145\t\n146\t| Agent | CLI | Input Method |\n147\t|-------|-----|-------------|\n148\t| Claude Code | `claude --print` | stdin |\n149\t| OpenCode | `opencode` | file |\n150\t| Codex CLI | `codex` | args |\n151\t| Aider | `aider --message` | args |\n152\t| *Custom* | *any* | *configurable via YAML adapter* |\n153\t\n154\tAdding a new agent requires **only a YAML configuration file** — no code changes.\n155\t\n156\t---\n157\t\n158\t## 📁 Repository Structure\n159\t\n160\t```\n161\tNEEDLE/\n162\t├── README.md\n163\t├── plan/\n164\t│   └── plan.md                     # Complete implementation plan\n165\t└── docs/\n166\t    ├── research/                   # Beads ecosystem research (14 files)\n167\t    └── notes/                      # NEEDLE v1 post-mortem learnings (9 files)\n168\t```\n169\t\n170\t---\n171\t\n172\t## 🔍 Observability\n173\t\n174\tNEEDLE emits structured telemetry for every state transition, claim attempt, dispatch, and outcome. A silent worker is a broken worker.\n175\t\n176\t### Exported Signals\n177\t\n178\t| Signal | Description |\n179\t|--------|-------------|\n180\t| **Traces** | Spans for `worker.session`, `bead.lifecycle`, `bead.claim`, `agent.dispatch`, `strand.evaluated`, `outcome.handled` |\n181\t| **Metrics** | `needle.beads.completed`, `needle.beads.duration`, `needle.agent.tokens.input`, `needle.cost.usd`, and more |\n182\t| **Logs** | All events not represented as spans, with severity mapping (`ERROR` for failures, `WARN` for stale peers) |\n183\t\n184\t### OpenTelemetry (OTLP) Export\n185\t\n186\tNEEDLE can export telemetry to any OpenTelemetry-compatible backend (Jaeger, Tempo, Grafana, Honeycomb, Datadog, etc.) via OTLP.\n187\t\n188\t**Minimal configuration (`.needle.yaml`):**\n189\t\n190\t```yaml\n191\ttelemetry:\n192\t  otlp_sink:\n193\t    enabled: true\n194\t    endpoint: \"http://localhost:4317\"  # gRPC, or :4318 for HTTP\n195\t    protocol: \"grpc\"\n196\t```\n197\t\n198\t**Semantic conventions:** NEEDLE follows OpenTelemetry's `gen_ai.*` semantic conventions for LLM telemetry, enabling out-of-the-box integration with GenAI dashboards (Grafana GenAI app, Langfuse, Honeycomb AI, etc.).\n199\t\n200\tSee [`docs/plan/plan.md`](docs/plan/plan.md) for the complete semantic mapping table.\n201\t\n202\t---\n203\t\n204\t## 📄 License\n205\t\n206\tMIT\n207\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3012bfad-6981-4a67-8009-22250c533afe","uuid":"b36d5aac-d6b6-4bb0-b72c-bd41fc18b04a","timestamp":"2026-04-26T11:13:15.947Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/coding/NEEDLE/README.md","content":"# 🧵 NEEDLE\n\n**N**avigates **E**very **E**nqueued **D**eliverable, **L**ogs **E**ffort\n\n> Deterministic bead processing with explicit outcome paths.\n\nNEEDLE is a universal wrapper for headless coding CLI agents. OpenTelemetry Collector Example\n\nThis example demonstrates how to receive NEEDLE telemetry via OTLP and visualize it with open-source observability tools.\n\n## Quick Start\n\n1. **Start the observability stack:**\n\n```bash\ncd docs/examples/otel-collector\ndocker-compose up -d\n```\n\nThis starts:\n- **OpenTelemetry Collector** (ports 4317/gRPC, 4318/HTTP)\n- **Jaeger** (UI: http://localhost:16686) — trace visualization\n- **Prometheus** (UI: http://localhost:9090) — metrics storage\n- **Loki** (port 3100) — log aggregation\n- **Grafana** (UI: http://localhost:3000, admin/admin) — unified dashboards\n\n2. **Configure NEEDLE to export OTLP:**\n\nIn your workspace `.needle.yaml`:\n\n```yaml\ntelemetry:\n  otlp_sink:\n    enabled: true\n    endpoint: \"http://localhost:4317\"\n    protocol: \"grpc\"\n```\n\n3. **Start NEEDLE:**\n\n```bash\nneedle work --workspace /path/to/workspace\n```\n\n4. **View the data:**\n\n| What | URL |\n|------|-----|\n| Traces | http://localhost:16686 (Jaeger UI) |\n| Metrics | http://localhost:9090 (Prometheus UI) |\n| Logs | http://localhost:3000 (Grafana with Loki data source) |\n| Dashboard | http://localhost:3000 (Grafana) |\n\n## Verifying Data Flow\n\n1. **Check collector health:**\n```bash\ncurl http://localhost:8888/metrics\n```\n\n2. **Query NEEDLE metrics in Prometheus:**\n```promql\nrate(needle_beads_completed_total[5m])\nhistogram_quantile(0.95, needle_beads_duration_ms_bucket)\n```\n\n3. **Search traces in Jaeger:**\n- Service: `needle`\n- Operation: any (or filter by `bead.lifecycle`, `agent.dispatch`, etc.)\n\n4. **View logs in Grafana:**\n- Add Loki data source: http://loki:3100\n- Query: `{job=\"needle\"}`\n\n## Stopping\n\n```bash\ndocker-compose down\n```\n\n## Customization\n\n- **Change endpoints:** Edit `docker-compose.yml` port mappings\n- **Add more backends:** Edit `otel-collector-config.yaml` to add exporters (e.g., Tempo, Honeycomb, Datadog)\n- **Adjust resource limits:** Add `mem_limit` and `cpus` to services in `docker-compose.yml`\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n- **No traces in Jaeger:** Check that NEEDLE is using the correct endpoint (4317 for gRPC, 4318 for HTTP)\n- **Collector logs:** `docker-compose logs -f otel-collector`\n- **Port conflicts:** Ensure ports 16686, 9090, 3000, 4317, 4318 are
